<p><b>Acehnese</b> or <b>Achinese</b> (<a href="/wiki/Jawi_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Jawi alphabet">Jawoë</a>: <span title="Acehnese-language text"><span lang="ace-Arab" dir="rtl"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1206473241"><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 125%;">بهسا اچيه</span>&#8206;</span></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian language</a> natively spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Acehnese_people" title="Acehnese people">Acehnese people</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. This language is also spoken by Acehnese descendants in some parts of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> like <a href="/wiki/Yan,_Kedah" class="mw-redirect" title="Yan, Kedah">Yan</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Kedah" title="Kedah">Kedah</a>.  Acehnese is used as the co-official language in the province of <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a>, Indonesia. Besides Indonesian used as the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 1988, <i>Acehnese</i> is the modern <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> name spelling and the bibliographical standard, and <a href="/wiki/Acehnese_people" title="Acehnese people">Acehnese people</a> use the spelling <i>Acehnese</i> when writing in English. <i>Achinese</i> is an antiquated spelling of the English language tradition. <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Atjehnese</i></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> spelling and an outdated <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> one. The spelling <i>Achehnese</i> originates from a 1906 English translation of the Dutch-language <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Studien over atjesche klank- en schriftleer. Tijdschrift voor Indische Taal-, Land- en Volkenkunde 35.346-442</i></span> by <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Snouck_Hurgronje" title="Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje">Christiaan Snouck Hurgronje</a>, 1892. In Acehnese the language is called <span title="Acehnese-language romanization"><i lang="ace-Latn">Basa/Bahsa Acèh</i></span>. In Indonesian it is called <span title="Indonesian-language text"><i lang="id">Bahasa Aceh</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_and_related_languages">Classification and related languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Classification and related languages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Acehnese belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian_languages" title="Malayo-Polynesian languages">Malayo-Polynesian branch</a> of <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a>. Acehnese's closest relatives are the other <a href="/wiki/Chamic_languages" title="Chamic languages">Chamic languages</a>, which are principally spoken in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>. The distant relative of the Chamic family is the <a href="/wiki/Malayic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayic language">Malayic language</a> family, which includes languages also spoken in <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_language" title="Minangkabau language">Minangkabau</a> as well as the national language, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Paul_Sidwell" title="Paul Sidwell">Paul Sidwell</a> notes that Acehnese likely has an <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic</a> substratum.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Linguist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Sidwell" title="Paul Sidwell">Paul Sidwell</a> wrote that "Sometime during this early phase of language shift, perhaps before the beginning of Common Era, the Chamic speakers who were to become the Acehnese left the mainland on a journey that would ultimately end in northern Sumatra." Basing on <a href="/wiki/Graham_Thurgood" title="Graham Thurgood">Graham Thurgood</a>'s thesis, Sidwell argues that Acehnese likely had been long separated from Chamic around the first to second century BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Distribution"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Peuta_Narit_Aceh.GIF" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Peuta_Narit_Aceh.GIF/220px-Peuta_Narit_Aceh.GIF" decoding="async" width="220" height="261" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Peuta_Narit_Aceh.GIF/330px-Peuta_Narit_Aceh.GIF 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/76/Peuta_Narit_Aceh.GIF 2x" data-file-width="380" data-file-height="450" /></a><figcaption>Regencies in <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a> with Acehnese language majority</figcaption></figure>
<p>Acehnese language is spoken primarily in coastal region of Aceh. This language is spoken in thirteen regencies and four cities in Aceh, which are:
</p><p><b>City</b>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Sabang,_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabang, Indonesia">Sabang</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Banda_Aceh" title="Banda Aceh">Banda Aceh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lhokseumawe" title="Lhokseumawe">Lhokseumawe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Langsa" title="Langsa">Langsa</a></li></ol>
<p><b>North-East Coast</b>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Aceh_Besar_Regency" title="Aceh Besar Regency">Aceh Besar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pidie_Regency" title="Pidie Regency">Pidie</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pidie_Jaya_Regency" title="Pidie Jaya Regency">Pidie Jaya</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bireuen_Regency" class="mw-redirect" title="Bireuen Regency">Bireuen</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Aceh_Regency" title="North Aceh Regency">North Aceh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_Aceh_Regency" title="East Aceh Regency">East Aceh</a> (except in three districts, Serba Jadi, Peunaron and Simpang Jernih, where the <a href="/wiki/Gayo_language" title="Gayo language">Gayo language</a> is spoken)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aceh_Tamiang_Regency" title="Aceh Tamiang Regency">Aceh Tamiang</a> (Mostly Manyak Payet and Kuala Simpang District; the rest of the Regency speaks a variety of the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayan languages">Malay language</a>)</li></ol>
<p><b>West-South Coast</b>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Aceh_Jaya_Regency" title="Aceh Jaya Regency">Aceh Jaya</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Aceh_Regency" title="West Aceh Regency">West Aceh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nagan_Raya_Regency" title="Nagan Raya Regency">Nagan Raya</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southwest_Aceh_Regency" title="Southwest Aceh Regency">Southwest Aceh</a> (except in Susoh District where the <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_language" title="Minangkabau language">Aneuk Jamee language</a> is spoken)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_Aceh_Regency" title="South Aceh Regency">South Aceh</a> (mixed with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Batak_language_Alas-Kluet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Batak language Alas-Kluet (page does not exist)">Kluet language</a> and Aneuk Jamee)</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Acehnese_phonology" title="Acehnese phonology">Acehnese phonology</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG/220px-Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG/330px-Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG/440px-Ie_Beuna_Narit_Aceh.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a><figcaption>Bilingual tsunami warning sign in Indonesian and Acehnese</figcaption></figure>

<p>In addition to the modern 26 letter <a href="/wiki/ISO_basic_Latin_alphabet" title="ISO basic Latin alphabet">basic Latin alphabet</a>, Acehnese uses the supplementary letters è, é, ë, ô, and ö, making a total of 31 letters in its orthography.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="636" /></a><figcaption>Hikayat Prang Sabi</figcaption></figure>

<p>Notes:
</p>
<ul><li>Syllable-final orthographic <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;k&#x27e9;</span> always represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔ/</span> save in certain recent loans</li>
<li><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> are borrowed sounds, and are often replaced by <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">d</span> and the clusters <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ph</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ch</span>, respectively</li>
<li>The nasals <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span> are realized as <a href="/wiki/Post-stopped_nasal" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-stopped nasal">post-stopped nasals</a> (also called "funny nasals") before oral vowels and consonants.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> They are distinct from the nasal-stop sequences <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mb/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nd/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲɟ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋɡ/</span>, e.g. in <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/banᵈa/</span> 'port' vs <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mandum/</span> 'all'.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Acehnese features a <a href="/wiki/Split_ergativity" title="Split ergativity">split ergative</a> system. Intransitives that align with the agent of a transitive verb (Sa) always show agreement by a proclitic (1). Meanwhile, intransitives that align with the patient of a transitive verb (Sp) may optionally show agreement by an enclitic (2). <a href="/wiki/Volition_(linguistics)" title="Volition (linguistics)">Volitionality</a> is the determining factor for whether an intransitive verb is Sa or Sp.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(1)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="ace" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Jih</p><p style="margin: 0px;">he</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="ace" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka=<b>ji</b>=jak.</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="inchoative aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INCHO</abbr>=<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3</abbr></b>=go</p></div><p style="display: none;">Jih ka=<b>ji</b>=jak.</p><p style="display: none;">he INCHO=<b>3</b>=go</p><p style="clear: left;">"He has gone."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(2)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="ace" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Gopnyan</p><p style="margin: 0px;">he</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="ace" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka=saket=<b>geuh</b>.</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="inchoative aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INCHO</abbr>=sick=<b><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3</abbr></b></p></div><p style="display: none;">Gopnyan ka=saket=<b>geuh</b>.</p><p style="display: none;">he INCHO=sick=<b>3</b></p><p style="clear: left;">"He is sick."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">Writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Writing system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Formerly, the Acehnese language was written in an <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic script</a> called Jawoë or <a href="/wiki/Jawi_script" title="Jawi script">Jawi</a> in the Malay language. The script is less common nowadays.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Since colonization by the Dutch, the Acehnese language has been written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>, with the addition of supplementary letters. The diacritical letters are é, è, ë, ö and ô.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The sound <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɨ/</span> is represented by <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;eu&#x27e9;</span> and the sound <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʌ/</span> is represented by <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ö&#x27e9;</span>, respectively. The letter 'ë' is used exclusively to represent the <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a> sound which forms the second part of diphthongs. The letters f, q, v, x, and z are only used in loanwords.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Literature"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Acehnese language is rich with literature. The oldest manuscript written in Acehnese is Hikayat Seumau'un from 1658 CE. Most Acehnese literatures consist of poetic works, very little written in prose form.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dialects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At least ten Achehnese dialects exist: Pasè, Peusangan, Matang, Pidië, Buëng, Banda, Daya,  Meulabôh, Seunagan, and Tunong.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acehnese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sample text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following texts are excerpts from the official translations of article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> in Acehnese, along with the original declaration in English.
</p>
<ul><li><i><b>Acehnese text sample:</b></i></li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd><b>Latin script</b><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd>"<span title="Acehnese-language text"><i lang="ace">Bandum ureuëng lahé deungon meurdéhka, dan deungon martabat dan hak njang saban. Ngon akai geuseumiké, ngon haté geumeurasa, bandum geutanjoë lagèë sjèëdara. Hak dan keumuliaan</i></span>."</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b>The original English version of the text:</b><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>"All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood."</dd></dl></dd></dl>

			<div class="thumb" style="width: 151.33333333333px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Hikayat Prang Sabi"><img alt="Hikayat Prang Sabi" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg/227px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg" decoding="async" width="152" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg/340px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg/453px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Handgeschreven_boek_in_Acehs_schrift_TMnr_2454-4a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="636" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Hikayat Prang Sabi</div>
		</li>
</ul>
